"--Wash</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_7072300">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7072300" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/416390-paul-bryant" class="left imgcol" title="Paul Bryant"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1224113172p2/416390.jpg" alt="Paul Bryant" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/7072300?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 23, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/416390-paul-bryant" class="user" title="Paul Bryant">Paul Bryant</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone with an insatiable interest in every possible detail about every possible person</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/416390-paul-bryant?shelf=really-big-timeconsumers" class="actionLinkLite">really-big-timeconsumers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/416390-paul-bryant?shelf=novels" class="actionLinkLite">novels</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/416390-paul-bryant?shelf=india" class="actionLinkLite">india</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer7072300">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4707087652745013546">After about page 200 I realised this was like eating Turkish Delight morning noon and night and my spiritual teeth were beginning to dissolve under a tide of sickliness which didn't ever let up. All these characters are so unbearably cute, even the less-nice ones. If post-independent India was crossed with Bambi, it would be Vikram Seth's endless gurgling prose.<br /> So I stopped reading and drove several three inch nails into my head, and I've been all right since then.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_855197753">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/855197753" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/15736557-lynne-king" class="left imgcol" title="Lynne King"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1357126217p2/15736557.jpg" alt="Lynne King" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/855197753?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 08, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/15736557-lynne-king" class="user" title="Lynne King">Lynne King</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/15736557-lynne-king?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/15736557-lynne-king?shelf=india" class="actionLinkLite">india</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/15736557-lynne-king?shelf=2014-books-to-be-read" class="actionLinkLite">2014-books-to-be-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer855197753">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11729195482012209372">This is a magnificent saga, which left me breathless and awaiting the next word, set in India at the beginning of the fifties.<br /><br />"Suitable Boy" by Vikram Seth's “epic love story set in India. Funny and tragic, with engaging, brilliantly observed characters, it is as close as you can get to Dickens for the twentieth century. The story unfolds through four middle class families - the Mehras, Kappoors, Khans and Chatterjis. Lata Mehra, a university student, is under pressure from her mother to get mar</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11729195482012209372">This is a magnificent saga, which left me breathless and awaiting the next word, set in India at the beginning of the fifties.<br /><br />"Suitable Boy" by Vikram Seth's “epic love story set in India. Funny and tragic, with engaging, brilliantly observed characters, it is as close as you can get to Dickens for the twentieth century. The story unfolds through four middle class families - the Mehras, Kappoors, Khans and Chatterjis. Lata Mehra, a university student, is under pressure from her mother to get married. But not to just anyone she happens to fall in love with. There are standards to be met and finding a husband for Lata becomes a family affair in which all the members are to play a part.”<br /><br />“The richness of this book is remarkable. What with marriage, religion, customs, etc. it has been a really fascinating read for me.”<br /><br />India's caste system has four main classes (also called varnas) based originally on personality, profession and birth. <br /><br />I’m eternally grateful to Fionnuala for suggesting that I may perhaps like this author. Do I like Vikram Seth? No, of course not. I just happen to adore him. I think that he’s absolutely splendid. I get the same pleasure reading this book as when I’m eating lobster or tasting a superb Burgundy wine or whatever sublime other pleasures that we have in life…My…<br /><br />I must confess that I had never heard of Seth before and I wouldn’t if it hadn’t been for Goodreads. It’s one of those remarkable books that becomes a reference book that once read, you can open it at any page and still get that continual enjoyment. It’s a wonderful sensation to savour…<br /><br />It’s always so difficult for me to write a review on a book that I “love to death” but that has been the case here. This is now my second favourite fiction book after “The Alexandria Quartet” and I could never do that justice. Bravo for the past for Durrell and for the present for Vikram Seth.<br /><br />In conclusion, Fionnuala and Seth – thank you for giving me so much pleasure. What a serendipitous find. I love this book.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11729195482012209372">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_226990793">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226990793" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1415047-whitaker" class="left imgcol" title="Whitaker"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1410926609p2/1415047.jpg" alt="Whitaker" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/226990793?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 16, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1415047-whitaker" class="user" title="Whitaker">Whitaker</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1415047-whitaker?shelf=contemporary-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1415047-whitaker?shelf=recommended-unreservedly" class="actionLinkLite">recommended-unreservedly</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1415047-whitaker?shelf=would-kill-if-thrown" class="actionLinkLite">would-kill-if-thrown</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1415047-whitaker?shelf=india" class="actionLinkLite">india</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1415047-whitaker?shelf=2011-read" class="actionLinkLite">2011-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1415047-whitaker?shelf=3965p-box1" class="actionLinkLite">3965p-box1</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer226990793">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6702630758947329524">I know some GR’ers didn’t really cotton on to the style of this book. And maybe it was because I read this while on vacation in India itself, but wow! Just W.O.W! It’s a fucking long book—1,500 pages. And every single page was worth the time I spent on it and more. <br /><br />If <em>Midnight’s Children</em> is India’s <em>One Hundred Years of Solitude</em>, then <em>A Suitable Boy</em> must be its <em>War and Peace</em>. It’s got the same melding of personal lives seen in amidst great national events. Instead of the romance of Natasha and Pi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6702630758947329524">I know some GR’ers didn’t really cotton on to the style of this book. And maybe it was because I read this while on vacation in India itself, but wow! Just W.O.W! It’s a fucking long book—1,500 pages. And every single page was worth the time I spent on it and more. <br /><br />If <em>Midnight’s Children</em> is India’s <em>One Hundred Years of Solitude</em>, then <em>A Suitable Boy</em> must be its <em>War and Peace</em>. It’s got the same melding of personal lives seen in amidst great national events. Instead of the romance of Natasha and Pierre, it’s that of Lata and her three suitors. Instead of the war with France, we have the post-Independence and post-Partition politics of a nation searching for an identity. And instead of descriptions of war, we get exchanges of heated debate on the floor of the state parliament, and the passing of a contentious bill. <br /><br />Seth looks at the lives of four families intertwined by marriage and friendship. And all the detail—and it is indeed loving detail—is very very necessary to immerse you in the India of the 1950s, and what it felt like to be alive then. We get details of village life, life in the city, life of the different castes, business life, religious life, modern life, traditional life. It’s all there. And it works in tandem with several great stories of love and passion, and what these mean, both at the level of family, romance, and nation. <br /><br />Word has it that Seth is working on a follow up (not sure if it’s a sequel as such) to be called “A Suitable Girl”. I, for one, can’t wait. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6702630758947329524">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1455762482">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455762482" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda" class="left imgcol" title="Arah-Lynda"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450281466p2/5859453.jpg" alt="Arah-Lynda" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1455762482?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5859453-arah-lynda" class="user" title="Arah-Lynda">Arah-Lynda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5859453-arah-lynda?shelf=i-said" class="actionLinkLite">i-said</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1455762482">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8213906521667985041">I finished Vikram Seth’s tome <strong>A Suitable Boy</strong> this Sunday morning while enjoying my coffee and a white chocolate, coconut Christmas cookie that my daughter had baked just last night. All right, all right, I confess it was actually two white chocolate, coconut Christmas cookies. But who can blame me really. They were so good. Not too sweet, she had gone ahead and reduced the suggested amount of sugar, resulting in a perfect blend of sweet with just a hint of salt and a nice moist and chewy texture</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8213906521667985041">I finished Vikram Seth’s tome <strong>A Suitable Boy</strong> this Sunday morning while enjoying my coffee and a white chocolate, coconut Christmas cookie that my daughter had baked just last night. All right, all right, I confess it was actually two white chocolate, coconut Christmas cookies. But who can blame me really. They were so good. Not too sweet, she had gone ahead and reduced the suggested amount of sugar, resulting in a perfect blend of sweet with just a hint of salt and a nice moist and chewy texture. And just the right size, one is not enough but two, hmmmmmm just right. Yum yum. <br /><br /><br />I wish I could say that this book also displayed just the right balance. Set in the early 1950’s in a newly independent India, <strong>A Suitable Boy</strong> focuses on the lives of four large families, connected by marriage or friendship, though most notably that of Lata Mehra, whose mother Mrs. Rupa Mehra, is intent on conducting an agonizing (hers) search, that pulls in all members of her immediate and extended family, to find a suitable husband for Lata. <br /><br />The story immerses you into the daily details of these families’ lives and indeed of India at that time and place. No stone is left unturned and no player too insignificant to escape the authors unquestionable skill in drawing rich characterizations and beautifully imagined settings. Through these people the reader is swept into a multiethnic society during an unsettling time of religious fervour and political unrest. It is all here: love, beauty, squalor, hatred, the caste system, prejudice, appalling violence and heart stopping tenderness. <br /><br />For me however there was just way too much detail. I really did not need to dive so deeply into the political manoeuvrings involved in passing a bill or the entire history of their philosophic or cultural rituals. There was so much detail, so deeply layered into the story that it detracted from, rather than enhanced my enjoyment of it. I found myself remembering John Galt’s speech way too often. I mean there is such a thing as too much icing on what is an already delicious cinnamon bun. <br /><br /><br />It is unfortunate, I believe that the editors did not cut some of that detail away, allowing the story to blossom in its own right as my daughter did with the sugar in her cookie recipe. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8213906521667985041">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown">
    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_17598610">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17598610" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/986856-sim" class="left imgcol" title="Sim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1206549290p2/986856.jpg" alt="Sim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/17598610?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 04, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/986856-sim" class="user" title="Sim">Sim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone! </span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer17598610'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer17598610">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13032279903695220542">*Spoiler alert*<br /><br />I finally finished reading A Suitable Boy by Vikram Seth. For some reason, I used to avoid picking it up and kept putting it off. I suppose it was mainly the size (it’s one thick book - approximately 1500 pages!) but I also think it had to do with this misconception I had that it would be a tough read, that Seth’s writing would be pompous and saturated with flowery descriptions of rivers winding through the green and yellow village of GraamNagar. Imagine my surprise when I find th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13032279903695220542">*Spoiler alert*<br /><br />I finally finished reading A Suitable Boy by Vikram Seth. For some reason, I used to avoid picking it up and kept putting it off. I suppose it was mainly the size (it’s one thick book - approximately 1500 pages!) but I also think it had to do with this misconception I had that it would be a tough read, that Seth’s writing would be pompous and saturated with flowery descriptions of rivers winding through the green and yellow village of GraamNagar. Imagine my surprise when I find that the language is smooth, his tone light and his narrative interesting. The fact that Seth managed to keep the threads of the numerous plots and subplots clear in his head is an accomplishment in itself, but even more impressive is how each characters of his story is real; they are people we recognize, with mannerisms we’ve noticed in ourselves and others, and dialogues we’ve heard, thought or spoken. <br /><br />The title might suggest that it’s the story of finding the perfect marriage candidate for the central character but that would be belittling the grand work that is A Suitable Boy. It is the story of the Mehras, the Kapoors, the Khans, the Chatterjis and a myriad of other characters, such as Saeeda Bai and Kakoli, many of whom are fleshed out substantially, even when their appearance is minimal. The beauty of the story arises from their interactions with each other, their thoughts and their ups and downs. Little details that create vivid images of a decaying courtesan’s world, a cosmopolitan Calcutta, the shoemakers’ rank (as in rancid) neighbourhoods and so on. The story covers about a year of the characters’ lives, detailing the day to day mundanity. Little decisions — a smile here, a letter there, a glass of nimbu pani (lemon-water) every now and then - are what makes the story. Yet these little decisions, these microsteps that are taken, culminate in huge changes that are noticed only in hindsight.<br /><br />I’m probably not giving away any surprises when I say that I was thoroughly pissed off at Lata Mehra’s decision to marry Haresh Khanna. I shouldn’t have been surprised because Lata does say in the first few pages, ” I always obey my mother” and so the ending wasn’t so much a surprise as it was a disappointment. I did understand why she did it, but I couldn’t help my acute disappointment in her all the same. I was genuinely frustrated at her pigheadedness, her thought process that led her to this decision. I was angry because I am afraid that her reasoning resonated with the coward in everyone, especially south asian girls who have had to, or will have to, at least discuss the concept of arranged marriage at some point in their lives.<br /><br />Ironically, her mother later suffered a number of qualms herself about whether Haresh would be the right boy for her daughter. Had Lata decided against the marriage, Mrs. Mehra would have been perfectly amenable, especially since Lata’s yuppie brother Arun did not condone the marriage either. So why did Lata decide to snub both Kabir, the Muslim she fell in love with, or Amit, the Bengali poet she could fall in love with easily? Her reasoning in the last few pages was scary because it reminded me of how we would rather our lives be a smooth ride of mediocrity than a roller coaster of brilliance that plummets from time to time. We choose to be mediocre-ly happy - the utilitarian idea that the “aim of action should be the largest possible balance of pleasure over pain or the greatest happiness of the greatest number” (<a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.m-w.com" target="_blank">http://www.m-w.com</a>). <br /><br />She says, “I’m not myself when I’m with him [Kabir]. I ask myself, who is this - this jealous, obsessed woman….I don’t want to [passionately love him], I don’t know want to. If that’s what passion means, I dont’ want it.”<br /><br />Once Lata makes her decision, we know that she will lead her life contently enough. It upset me because I saw Lata in a number of people I know in real life, including myself. Mind you, I am not advocating against arranged marriage as a whole because I know they can work. Lata’s sister Savita, who marries Pran after meeting him only once in front of her elders, does genuinely fall in love with him and go on to lead a happy life. So it’s not that arranged marriages are wrong. I just felt that Lata was wrong in her decision to marry Haresh. Even if he was considered fair and good looking, confident and ambitious. Ironically, from Haresh’s side, it’s not exactly a traditional arranged marriage. He arranges his nuptials himself because he doesn’t like the parents getting involved in this matter; his parents already know that he will run away (metaphorically speaking) if they try to set him up. So to Haresh, this is a decision he’s making by himself for his own benefit. Haresh had already been in love with someone else before, had neatly folded away his Devdas romanticism for that girl and was ready now to live a contented life with someone else (it just happened to be Lata). He is oh so bloody honest about his feelings for this girl, and that he knows it won’t ever happen and so must move on… Lata wanted his practicality, his forceful ability to get things done, his willingness to help out her family members. What angered me was the underlying assumption that Kabir/Amit couldn’t be all those things, that they would be selfish beings simply because they would also love her, and she would have to him (either him) back. <br /><br />My favourite characters in the book are Amit Chatterji and Pran Kapoor. I know Vikram Seth denies fashioning Amit after him, but to be honest, for some reason while I was reading about Amit’s tendencies for the necessary inactivity that comes with being a writer, I thought of Seth. What I liked about Amit was that he was the uber intellectual: his tone was oft-sardonic, his amusement frequent, his observations of people accepting and piercing. He talked a lot and said very little. He was cryptic in his cynicism. I loved him. Lata rejects him on the basis of his being "high-maintenance" type - someone who needs his meals laid out for him, who wouldn’t have time for her if he was working on a novel, and whose moodswings are as frequent as her own. I don’t buy that completely. He did make the time for her, he knew how to be charming and behave in society (he wasn’t an absent-minded intellectual), he knew what he wanted and he knew how to get what he wants. Lata was right in that he wouldn’t fall apart at her rejection, but I think it’s not his insensitivity that would allow him to be friends with her after her marriage, but his excessive civility, his sophistication and his writer’s acceptance of life.<br /><br />My other favourite character, Pran Kapoor - a thin, dark quiet professor - is a sweetheart. The kind of nice guy who doesn’t begrudge his mother-in-law’s long vacations with them, who plays April Fools Day jokes on people because “those who aren’t conscious of the date must take the consequences”. He is the ultimate good son, who quietly accepts his arranged marriage and falls in love with his wife. His was the real arranged marriage, in the true sense of the word, and yet you cannot dislike him or his wife Savita because they are both so lovable people, that you just know that they were destined to be together, no matter how they got together.<br /><br />For those of you who haven’t read it, do. Trust me, I can’t begin to describe the many shades there are to each character and how nothing I say will completely do justice to them. I got mad at one character’s one decision, not at the book. Seth is amazing. His voice is uninstrusive and style very graceful. That’s the word: graceful. Despite its size, you get a soft feeling reading it. True it is a tad tedious at times. Some of the political parts and some of the characters could have been done without. But in the end, you can’t get angry at someone who gives you the whole cake when all you asked for was a slice.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13032279903695220542">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1822332">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14260251919889134245">Vikram Seth's A Suitable Boy is one of the best books I've ever read in my entire life. It's a long book. But it is very engaging; I managed to read it in one stretch, with a break to sleep, while I awaited the movers to take me and my belongings across the counry. To my chagrin I had completed it before my flight, and when it finished I didn't want the book to be over, I wanted to go back and re-read it from the beginning. It is one of the best books about life in India I've ever read, it is th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14260251919889134245">Vikram Seth's A Suitable Boy is one of the best books I've ever read in my entire life. It's a long book. But it is very engaging; I managed to read it in one stretch, with a break to sleep, while I awaited the movers to take me and my belongings across the counry. To my chagrin I had completed it before my flight, and when it finished I didn't want the book to be over, I wanted to go back and re-read it from the beginning. It is one of the best books about life in India I've ever read, it is the anti-Kite Runner book. There is nothing trite or stereotyped about the characterization; it believably describes elements of society that are even oblique to people with the mainstream of modern Indian society; the plot is not simple, nor is it a convulted mystery story. <br /><br />Writing this up I think I should go get it and read it again. Like most of my favorite books I gave it away a long time ago.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_133354753">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133354753" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3642045-sue" class="left imgcol" title="Sue"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1274829293p2/3642045.jpg" alt="Sue" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/133354753?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 23, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3642045-sue" class="user" title="Sue">Sue</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone interested in India and historical fiction</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=india" class="actionLinkLite">india</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3642045-sue?shelf=read-2014" class="actionLinkLite">read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer133354753">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4971592061124636016">A Suitable Boy takes place over the course of a year in an India which is adjusting not only to independence but to partition. Through the stories of some of the major families of Brahmpur, we observe and participate in not only the day to day activities of individuals but the workings of government, developing industry--some quite primitive, the existence of caste--though outlawed, religious hatred, and the search for love and marriage. There are beauty and violence, squalor and humor, festival</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4971592061124636016">A Suitable Boy takes place over the course of a year in an India which is adjusting not only to independence but to partition. Through the stories of some of the major families of Brahmpur, we observe and participate in not only the day to day activities of individuals but the workings of government, developing industry--some quite primitive, the existence of caste--though outlawed, religious hatred, and the search for love and marriage. There are beauty and violence, squalor and humor, festivals and riots. It is a very full year.<br /><br />At the center is Lata, searching for that "suitable" boy, the man she will marry.That quest is not finalized until the end of the novel and is worth reading about but so much more is happening. I came to this book with a smattering of knowledge about India and Indian beliefs and customs and come away with a feeling that I have learned enough to want to know more. This is a country both rich and poor: rich in tradition, rich in religious beliefs, rich in an amazing ability to pick itself up from disaster but poor in ability to distribute its wealth and to eliminate its history of castes (I do recognize that this novel is set in the 1950s), poor in eliminating government graft, and poor in eliminating inter-religious strife. All are on display here and have not been eliminated today. (I will not hesitate to say that the country I live in, and most others have many of the same problems to one degree or another.)<br /><br />But family is at the center of this novel and Lata at the center of one family.<br /><br /><br /><em>[Lata] wondered what one could do to be born happy, to<br /> achieve happiness, or to have it thrust on one. The baby, <br /> she thought, had arranged to be born happy; she was placid,<br /> and had as good a chance as anyone of happiness in this<br /> world...Pran and Savita, different though their backgrounds<br /> were, were a happy couple. They recognized limits and<br /> possibilities; their yearnings did not stretch beyond their<br /> reach. They loved each other---or, rather, had come to do<br /> so. They both assumed, without ever needing to state it---<br /> or perhaps without even thinking explicitly about<br /> it---that marriage and children were a great good.</em><br /> ( pp 951-952)<br /><br /><br />This is one of the examples for Lata to observe. Of course there are other, some decidedly less functional.<br /><br />This book does require a major investment of time and attention but for those who give it, there is a great return. Personally I find well written historical fiction a wonderful road to explore another culture.<br /><br />Highly recommended!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4971592061124636016">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_6449803">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6449803" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/395503-danielle-franco-malone" class="left imgcol" title="Danielle Franco-Malone"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1264628096p2/395503.jpg" alt="Danielle Franco-Malone" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/6449803?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 02, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/395503-danielle-franco-malone" class="user" title="Danielle Franco-Malone">Danielle Franco-Malone</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/395503-danielle-franco-malone?shelf=dani-s-very-faves" class="actionLinkLite">dani-s-very-faves</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395503-danielle-franco-malone?shelf=dani-s-top-10" class="actionLinkLite">dani-s-top-10</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer6449803">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11830214853535885994">This is one of my five all time favorite books (along with the Handmaid's Tale, On Beauty, the Red Tent, &amp; Corelli's Mandolin). It is a patch work story of many characters' lives; by the end of the story, you see how they all intersect. <br /><br />This was one of those books where when I finished the book I was completely invested in each of the character's life. The story is set in post-independence India and explores a number of social/political issues of the time (i.e. land reform, muslim-hindu rela</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11830214853535885994">This is one of my five all time favorite books (along with the Handmaid's Tale, On Beauty, the Red Tent, &amp; Corelli's Mandolin). It is a patch work story of many characters' lives; by the end of the story, you see how they all intersect. <br /><br />This was one of those books where when I finished the book I was completely invested in each of the character's life. The story is set in post-independence India and explores a number of social/political issues of the time (i.e. land reform, muslim-hindu relations, women's rights, arranged marriage, the caste system), but the political commentary doesn't hit you over the head, and the characters really drive the story. <br /><br />Despite my enthusiastic recommendations, I've had a hard time finding anyone to read this book! At 1379 pages it is apparently the longest book to be printed in English in one volume. However I found it to be a total page turner. Just resign yourself to the fact that you'll be reading this book for a couple of months and give it a try. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11830214853535885994">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_849329339">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/849329339" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7481492-margitte" class="left imgcol" title="Margitte"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1361772481p2/7481492.jpg" alt="Margitte" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/849329339?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 02, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7481492-margitte" class="user" title="Margitte">Margitte</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=political-novel" class="actionLinkLite">political-novel</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=family" class="actionLinkLite">family</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=drama" class="actionLinkLite">drama</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=2014-read" class="actionLinkLite">2014-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=india" class="actionLinkLite">india</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer849329339">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9937065430446050266">The book blurb says it all. I will only add my comments.<br /><br />While reading this monumental novel of 1535 pages, I was wondering how much of the original offering was edited out to end up with this number of pages as the final result! I also wondered, while ploughing through it, how much of the existing book can be cut out and still leave the essential core. Probably half of it. Compared to Barbara Kingsolver and Yung Chang, Vikram Seth needed twice as much pages to tell similar stories as these two a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9937065430446050266">The book blurb says it all. I will only add my comments.<br /><br />While reading this monumental novel of 1535 pages, I was wondering how much of the original offering was edited out to end up with this number of pages as the final result! I also wondered, while ploughing through it, how much of the existing book can be cut out and still leave the essential core. Probably half of it. Compared to Barbara Kingsolver and Yung Chang, Vikram Seth needed twice as much pages to tell similar stories as these two authors.<br /><br />So yes, it was a long-winded journey: a story of India after Partition, that was told through the eyes of four extended families with each member profiled to the last red spot of <em>paan</em> on the teeth. This book really celebrates the good, the bad and the ugly of humankind. Mrs. Rupa Mehra, with her daughter,Lata, get the train rolling when it becomes time to find a suitable husband for Lata. India in all its colorful splendor is presented to the reader to almost the puking stage, to be really honest! But how fascinating the journey!<br /><br />Enough! Enough! Enough! I often wanted to just run away, and I did, since it is the end of the financial year (February) and what is normally a quiet relaxed month turned out to be one of the craziest in recent history. But each evening I sneaked off to bed and grabbed the book as though my life depended on it. <br /><br />In retrospect this book was amazing. The drama lasted the entire 1535 pages and that really makes this book outstanding! There's no villains, only ordinary people writing their own histories while living their lives. <br /><br />I do not want to add too much spoilers and blow the plot, or give away the story. But I cannot leave out one of the most outstanding moments in the book, for me: it was the passing of a mother and it had me crying like losing my own. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[<em>" She had dispersed. She was the garden at Prem Nivas (soon to be entered into the annual Flower Show), she was Veena's love of music, Pran's asthma, Maans generosity, the survival of some refugees four years ago, the neem leaves that would preserve quilts stored in the great zinc trunks of Prem Nivas, the moulting feathers of some pond herons, a small unrung brass bell, the memory of decency in an indecent time, the temperament of Bhaskar's great-grandchildren, indeed, for all the Minister of Revenue's impatience with her, she was his regret. And it was right that she should continue to be so, for he should have treated her better while she lived, the poor, ignorant, grieving fool."</em>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Much of India's modern history could have been my own country's. Even the name of political parties, the titles of new bills, the speeches made in parliament, the way landowners got treated, sounded like it was written for South Africa. Much of the events are disturbingly similar. In fact, it is a blueprint and it turned my stomach upside down. Not that it is a surprise, but it is still upsetting to experience.<br /><br />I liked this book. It was a brilliant presentation of Mother India and all her beautiful children.<br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9937065430446050266">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1480907890">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1480907890" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3144945-alex" class="left imgcol" title="Alex"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1303883046p2/3144945.jpg" alt="Alex" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1480907890?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 07, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3144945-alex" class="user" title="Alex">Alex</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=rth-lifetime" class="actionLinkLite">rth-lifetime</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=music" class="actionLinkLite">music</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=2016" class="actionLinkLite">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1480907890">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14817378221382188292"><em>Dynasty</em> in India is what this book really <a rel="nofollow" title="Lengthy NY Times piece where he says it himself" href="http://www.nytimes.com/1993/05/02/magazine/vikram-seth-s-big-book.html?pagewanted=all">is,</a> for all its allusions to Victorian novels. But sure, yes, it's longer than <a title="My review" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135613423">War &amp; Peace,</a> ensuring its place on the Books Your Friends Didn't Finish list:<br /><br /><strong>The <a rel="nofollow" title="A way to judge which books people finish least" href="http://www.wsj.com/articles/the-summers-most-unread-book-is-1404417569">Hawking Index</a></strong><br />- <a title="It's not briefer, actually" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91037254">Brief History of Time</a><br />- <a title="My review" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1499691738">Jonathan Strange &amp; Mr. Norrell</a><br />- Suitable Boy<br />- Every book published before 1940<br />- The Bible<br /><br />And it shares with War &amp; Peace a panoramic, many-charactered view of an entire society, against the backdrop of real events - here, the 1951 abolition of the f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14817378221382188292"><em>Dynasty</em> in India is what this book really <a rel="nofollow" title="Lengthy NY Times piece where he says it himself" href="http://www.nytimes.com/1993/05/02/magazine/vikram-seth-s-big-book.html?pagewanted=all">is,</a> for all its allusions to Victorian novels. But sure, yes, it's longer than <a title="My review" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135613423">War &amp; Peace,</a> ensuring its place on the Books Your Friends Didn't Finish list:<br /><br /><strong>The <a rel="nofollow" title="A way to judge which books people finish least" href="http://www.wsj.com/articles/the-summers-most-unread-book-is-1404417569">Hawking Index</a></strong><br />- <a title="It's not briefer, actually" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91037254">Brief History of Time</a><br />- <a title="My review" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1499691738">Jonathan Strange &amp; Mr. Norrell</a><br />- Suitable Boy<br />- Every book published before 1940<br />- The Bible<br /><br />And it shares with War &amp; Peace a panoramic, many-charactered view of an entire society, against the backdrop of real events - here, the 1951 abolition of the feudal Zamindari system, and the taut relationship between Hindus and Muslims in post-colonial India, which had just divided itself in two in order to pack most of its Muslims off to Pakistan.<br /><br />Vikram Seth's real love is for <a title="My review of Emma, my favorite and Lata's" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/806060806">Jane Austen,</a> though, and the major plot is pure Austen: whom will Lata Mehra marry? The suitors include ambitious Haresh, who reads pessimistic <a title="My review of Far from the Madding Crowd" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1314594412">Hardy;</a> the poet and Seth stand-in Amit Chatterji, who (along with Lata herself) reads Austen; and the Muslim Kabir, who is in no way suitable and does not read novels (but he does act in Shakespeare's Twelfth Night).<br /><br />The other major plotline involves the growing up of Lata's brother-in-law Maan Kapoor, who has an affair with musical courtesan Saeeda Bai. These two families, the Mehras and the Kapoors, twine together throughout the book, along with the Chatterjis and the Muslim Khans. It can get confusing. Here are the major characters:<br /><br />MEHRAS (Rupa &amp; dead husband)<br />Arun (business douche) -&gt; Meenakshi Chatterji<br />   daughter Aparna<br />Varun (milquetoast)<br />Savita -&gt; Pran Kapoor<br />Lata<br /><br />KAPOORS (Mahesh and Mrs.)<br />Pran (professor) -&gt; Savita Mehra<br />Maan (Saeeda Bai, best friends with Firoz Khan)<br />Veena -&gt; Kedarnath Tandon the shoe guy<br />   son Bhaskar is good at math<br /><br />KHANS (Nawab Sahib of Baitar)<br />Begun Abida Khan, sister-in-law politician<br />Zainab (daughter)<br />Imtiaz<br />Firoz (into Tasneem, Saeeda Bai's younger sister; best friends with Maan Kapoor)<br /><br />CHATTERJIS (Justice &amp; Mrs.)<br />Amit - poet<br />Meenakshi (a shitty person) -&gt; Arun Mehra<br />Dipankar (the religious one)<br />Kakoli (silly but fun)<br />Tapan (nobody cares about Tapan)<br /><br />EVERYONE ELSE<br />Saeeda Bai the singing courtesan &amp; her sister Tasneem - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[not a real sister <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />LN Agarwhal (incompetent politician)<br />Raja of Marh (asshole with gay son)<br />Dr. Durrani (Muslim mathematician)<br />Kabir Durrani (potential match for Lata)<br />Haresh (ambitious shoemaker, potential Lata match)<br />Malati (Lata's best friend)<br /><br />Whew. There are of course family trees at the beginning of the book that you should bookmark. My book club has also put together <a rel="nofollow" href="https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/17AoIwJ5EJR22TdmewQicNUdmYTx9tXqC0ON-bYK9Sx8/edit">a glossary</a> that may help you. (Thanks Kaion!) And I even made <a rel="nofollow" href="https://open.spotify.com/user/drdastardly/playlist/0W7Q3WVx1V97FYtsYUmuTm">a Suitable Playlist</a> on Spotify! It contains many of the songs mentioned in the book. The "Rise traveler, the sky is bright" song is Uth, Jaag, Musafir.<br /><br />That's a lot of stuff, and this is a lot of book. It'll fully immerse you in Indian culture, which is neat. It's not <em>difficult;</em> it's still a soap opera, with lots of gossip and plot, and Seth writes cleanly. I found it hard to put down when I was reading it, but sometimes hard to pick up again when I wasn't. It didn't really grab me in an "I can't wait to keep reading" way until around 75%. But I really liked it. Nothing wrong with an Indian Dynasty.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14817378221382188292">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_400933483">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400933483" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/83144-el" class="left imgcol" title="El"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452263504p2/83144.jpg" alt="El" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/400933483?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 22, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/83144-el" class="user" title="El">El</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=20th-centurylit-late" class="actionLinkLite">20th-centurylit-late</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=cultural-studies-and-other" class="actionLinkLite">cultural-studies-and-other</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=wanderlust" class="actionLinkLite">wanderlust</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=1001-books-list" class="actionLinkLite">1001-books-list</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=big-effing-books" class="actionLinkLite">big-effing-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=anarchism-revolutions" class="actionLinkLite">anarchism-revolutions</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=india" class="actionLinkLite">india</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer400933483">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17247261738949584644">For Thanksgiving 2010 I spent the day <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114821378">finishing up Infinite Jest</a>. For a while there I thought maybe I'd always try to finish up some sort of behemoth on Thanksgiving day, since the day to me means staying in my jammies and watching The Godfather on TV while I read. The food involved can easily be made while reading or the Boyfriend steps up and makes the yummies. But then last year I went with a <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239138408">a shorter book choice</a> which I was able to read all on Thanksgiving. Boy, was that a mistake.<br /><br />But then</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17247261738949584644">For Thanksgiving 2010 I spent the day <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114821378">finishing up Infinite Jest</a>. For a while there I thought maybe I'd always try to finish up some sort of behemoth on Thanksgiving day, since the day to me means staying in my jammies and watching The Godfather on TV while I read. The food involved can easily be made while reading or the Boyfriend steps up and makes the yummies. But then last year I went with a <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239138408">a shorter book choice</a> which I was able to read all on Thanksgiving. Boy, was that a mistake.<br /><br />But then it so happened that I wasn't able to finish <em>this</em> book when I had anticipated (which was about a month ago), so it wound up getting to be close to Thanksgiving. Could I finish it off on Turkey Day? You challenging me??<br /><br />Yeah, I finished it today. And it feels good. It's a different kind of feeling than what I experienced with Infinite Jest. A Suitable Boy is another whopper of a book, but even the parts I didn't necessarily understand still made more sense to me than most parts of Infinite Jest. Infinite Jest was <em>work</em>, albeit a fun flavor of work most of the time. A Suitable Boy felt like I was in a different country (hello, India!), totally immersed in the culture.<br /><br />When I get right down to it, that's what I have loved about A Suitable Boy - the flavor dripping from each page. This isn't just a story; it's an experience. The reader experiences the music, the food, the costumes, the scents, the emotions, the politics, and the family dynamics. I can't remember the last time I read a book with so many <em>layers</em>. I started out reading this alongside <a title="Freedom at Midnight by Larry Collins" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/204123.Freedom_at_Midnight">Freedom at Midnight</a>, hoping that book would help me understand some of the politics I didn't know much about going into it. And it did, probably more than I had originally expected.<br /><br />At first my biggest question was why Seth decided to write a book about the Republic of India in 1952, when it seems the logical (maybe laziest? easiest?) starting point should have been 1947, during the Partition. But then a couple things became obvious to me. One was that 1952 was an important year too, it was an election year. Anyone who pays attention to politics in our own country knows just how important an election year is, and just how effing crazy everything gets. That's not exclusive just to the United States. Now imagine it's the <em>first</em> national election after gaining independence. Yeah, that sounds crazy-making.<br /><br />The other thing that became obvious was what I read in the author bio at the beginning of the book (which, for some reason, I didn't read at first). Vikram Seth himself was born 1952. Now, maybe that's just a coincidence, but maybe it's not. Maybe Seth was writing his own personal history in these 1400+ pages. It's evident to me he poured his heart and soul into this work. Seems to me this was an important novel for him to write. Makes sense to me.<br /><br />Somewhere in all this political turmoil and unrest is a love story, or a few different love stories. There's a huge genealogy here - the family tree at the beginning of the book helps considerably, but an understanding of the entire tree is not completely necessary in enjoying the book. The chapters flow by easily, it's not a difficult read, aside from the fact that the book itself breaks your wrists as you hold it. As one reads, the genealogy comes together on its own. My point is, don't stress about it.<br /><br />I was most invested in Lata's story since that's where the title comes from and also I am a girl and sometimes find myself drawn towards other girls in literature. Lata and I have had completely different upbringings and family dynamics, but I can still relate to her on some level. She's an interesting character, and I believe she's the first woman in her family to have a sense of - and desire for - independence. Finding 'a suitable boy' and getting married is not her goal in life, not at this point. She's educated, going to college, she gets a part in a school play, she has some love interest(s), she's doing her own thing. She's doing <em>her</em>.<br /><br />But society isn't ready for that. With all of the changes the society is going through, fully independent women is not quite where it is yet in 1952. Lata's family isn't thrilled with it and ultimately Lata needs to make a decision with how she will proceed.<br /><br />Seth makes it all seem absolutely riveting. I don't know what else to say.<br /><br />Rumor has it (although I think it's beyond rumor stage at this point) that Seth is working on a sequel, A Suitable Girl. If it's anything as wonderful as A Suitable Boy I think we're all in for a treat. If, however, as I fear, he's just banking on the popularity of A Suitable Boy... then it could be quite the loser and snoozer. But he's won me over with this one and I will be excited to see what comes next. And, because I'm a serious nerd, I hope it's as much a whopper of a book as this one.<br /><blockquote>"Oh, I don't know how it grew to be so long," said Amit. "I'm very undisciplined. But I too hate long books: the better, the worse. If they're bad, they merely make me pant with the effort of holding them up for a few minutes. But if they're good, I turn into a social moron for days, refusing to go out of my room, scowling and growling at interruptions, ignoring weddings and funerals, and making enemies out of friends. I still bear the scars of Middlemarch."<br />(p 1370-71)</blockquote></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17247261738949584644">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_105359521">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105359521" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/426277-james" class="left imgcol" title="James"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1359650680p2/426277.jpg" alt="James" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/105359521?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 22, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/426277-james" class="user" title="James">James</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/426277-james?shelf=u-of-chicago" class="actionLinkLite">u-of-chicago</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/426277-james?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/426277-james?shelf=indian-lit" class="actionLinkLite">indian-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer105359521">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7317550176825462381">This is a novel of India set in the early 1950s just after the partition, Vikram Seth's <em>A Suitable Boy</em> provides a window into the culture and history of India at that juncture in its history through a romance about a young girl, Lata, whose mother, Mrs. Rupa Mehra, is searching for a "suitable boy" for her to marry. The novel's opening section succeeded in immediately arresting my attention. Some of the most notable aspects of the novel include the subtle ways that the author suggests the contin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7317550176825462381">This is a novel of India set in the early 1950s just after the partition, Vikram Seth's <em>A Suitable Boy</em> provides a window into the culture and history of India at that juncture in its history through a romance about a young girl, Lata, whose mother, Mrs. Rupa Mehra, is searching for a "suitable boy" for her to marry. The novel's opening section succeeded in immediately arresting my attention. Some of the most notable aspects of the novel include the subtle ways that the author suggests the continuing cultural influence of England, from the impact of literary awards to the reading habits of several of the characters. Moreover the novel successfully includes all aspects of Indian life and nationality from the caste system to religious differences between Hindus and Muslims to the impact of changes in business and government life on the four families at the center of the novel. Seth's novel is a tour de force that demonstrates his skill in writing, knowledge of India, and his ability to marry the charms of a classical romance novel within the broad reach of a realistic family and nationalistic saga. Without disclosing the plot details I can only assure the reader that it is worth all 1400 plus pages. The thematic development of the clash between Hindu and Muslim cultures is particularly well portrayed with the impact of historical events on the national level mirrored by dramatic events among the main families whose lives fill the plot and subplots of the novel. It is rare that such a long book is both an entertaining read and an intellectually satisfying challenge. Vikram Seth has succeeded in both areas. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7317550176825462381">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_26015081">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26015081" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/278284-quirine" class="left imgcol" title="Quirine"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Quirine" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/26015081?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 01, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/278284-quirine" class="user" title="Quirine">Quirine</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer26015081">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12479034768100783998">I have an in-built horror of books that stray on longer than 300 pages. Anything longer and I always find the story sagging somewhere towards the middle and losing me by the end. Except with A Suitable Boy. It's over 1000 (tightly written) pages and I only wish it could have gone on and on. This sprawling saga takes you all over India in the 50s, into the lives of a dozen or so interconnected characters. And yet Seth masterfully manages to keep each story bubbling on the stove with delicious res</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12479034768100783998">I have an in-built horror of books that stray on longer than 300 pages. Anything longer and I always find the story sagging somewhere towards the middle and losing me by the end. Except with A Suitable Boy. It's over 1000 (tightly written) pages and I only wish it could have gone on and on. This sprawling saga takes you all over India in the 50s, into the lives of a dozen or so interconnected characters. And yet Seth masterfully manages to keep each story bubbling on the stove with delicious results! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12479034768100783998">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_468928475">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/468928475" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/15134781-anoop-pai-b" class="left imgcol" title="Anoop Pai B"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1444446804p2/15134781.jpg" alt="Anoop Pai B" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/468928475?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 13, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/15134781-anoop-pai-b" class="user" title="Anoop Pai B">Anoop Pai B</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/10469712-a-suitable-boy" title="Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/15134781-anoop-pai-b?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/15134781-anoop-pai-b?shelf=4-to-5-stars" class="actionLinkLite">4-to-5-stars</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/15134781-anoop-pai-b?shelf=excess-fat" class="actionLinkLite">excess-fat</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/15134781-anoop-pai-b?shelf=tome-to-me" class="actionLinkLite">tome-to-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer468928475">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7591285514575077260">Game, set, match.. Cannot control my tears (not literal ones) from streaming down on my dust covered face and leaving a track as it slides down.. <br />Reading this book felt like lifting the Wimbledon trophy, the most coveted prize in tennis. Ever single person who turns a professional, wants to win nothing more, than Wimbledon, at least once. Else there is no inner peace. I too, was like a tennis player, in the sense that ever since I picked up a novel, ever since I became an "avid" reader, Suitable</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7591285514575077260">Game, set, match.. Cannot control my tears (not literal ones) from streaming down on my dust covered face and leaving a track as it slides down.. <br />Reading this book felt like lifting the Wimbledon trophy, the most coveted prize in tennis. Ever single person who turns a professional, wants to win nothing more, than Wimbledon, at least once. Else there is no inner peace. I too, was like a tennis player, in the sense that ever since I picked up a novel, ever since I became an "avid" reader, Suitable Boy was was my ultimate challenge. If ever there was one book that scared me yet pulled me towards it, it was this book.<br />And now that I have completed reading this book I am left with a void within myself. There is an unwelcomed emptiness inside of me that can be filled with only by another wonderful book, which alas, may take some time in finding.<br />In some ways, you can say that the book is like How I Met Your Mother. You know that the story is about how Ted meets his wife and also that his princess wont be revealed till last season. This book too is something like that. The first sentence reveals what the crux is going to be. but still you are left in amazement as to how Seth has managed to narrate it over 1300 pages without boring you at any place. I am still amazed.<br />The strength of the book lies in the simplicity of the narration and in the humble decoration of the characters. Nothing is loud or gaudy or chaotic, but it is simple, sweet and pleasant. Each and every character has a unique personality, distinct from one another. What this does is that it prevents the story from being monotonous and repetitive. <br />The story revolves around Lata, whose mother states an ultimatum of sorts, that she too will marry a guy chosen by the mother, just like her sister did. What follows is a journey on a train of beautiful storytelling with scenic characters passing by and you are left turning your head back to catch a final glimpse of each one of them.<br />Vikram Seth takes you to the place of Brahmapur where the story takes place (with an occasional visit to Calcutta, Delhi, Kanpur and other cities). One would get the feeling of being right amidst the members of the family and taking an active participation in their day to day chores, their joys, their sorrows, their struggles, their victory, their celebration, their tears, their hunger, their delight and so on. One might find it hard to express satisfaction or otherwise at the actions and reactions of the characters. Many a times, I was yelling into a book, almost talking to the characters when I knew that I was being ridiculous (or was I?). In fact, I went to through many sleepless nights because I just could not stop reading.<br />But as said in Matrix Revolutions, all that has a beginning has an end. Eventually I did have to put down the book. Eventually I had to say goodbye to all of the people whom I had met in the book, who became my kith and kin, who became more endearing to me than my actual relatives. I am not sad that book got over, but I am glad that I read this one.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7591285514575077260">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/14814032-bramha-raju" class="user" title="Bramha Raju">Bramha Raju</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer551770252">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5714313511284115368">I admit without a semblance of ignominy that my convent bred education never allowed me to enjoy my own clan- Indian authors. But recently, as my brother would say, I have developed a taste for it. When this book was released and made such a mayhem in the readers world, the size of the book and the language put me off. It has been sitting on my shelf and quietly staring at me until I couldn’t ignore it any longer. I finally read it and now at 37 years old and 13 years plus married life, I thorou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5714313511284115368">I admit without a semblance of ignominy that my convent bred education never allowed me to enjoy my own clan- Indian authors. But recently, as my brother would say, I have developed a taste for it. When this book was released and made such a mayhem in the readers world, the size of the book and the language put me off. It has been sitting on my shelf and quietly staring at me until I couldn’t ignore it any longer. I finally read it and now at 37 years old and 13 years plus married life, I thoroughly empathize with the protagonist, Lata. Lata’s decision was no surprise. I saw it coming. Still I was angry and badly upset. Maybe because I could resonate with her reasoning. Maybe because I am reminded of the coward in me? Maybe because she speaks for the large mass of girls who would rather their lives be a smooth ride of mediocrity than the brilliance of quicksilver. Choosing to be mediocrely happy. Choosing the safer path, choosing the content life, choosing the stagnation. Lata disturbed me and I know it’s going to take some time to get back to my mediocrely safe choices. But all in all it was a brilliant read and Vikrem Seth is a graceful writer. Almost like a Jane Austen. He is too elaborative at times and hopefully forgive me for skipping a few pages on parliamentary politics. So when Vikram Seth challenges you in his opening lines.. <br /><br />'Buy me before good sense insists,<br />You’ll strain your purse and sprain your wrists.'<br /><br />take the plunge. Its worth your time. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5714313511284115368">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
