<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1300139222">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1300139222" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1926708-rebecca" class="left imgcol" title="Rebecca"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1409715482p2/1926708.jpg" alt="Rebecca" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1300139222?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1926708-rebecca" class="user" title="Rebecca">Rebecca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1926708-rebecca?shelf=read-in-2015" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1926708-rebecca?shelf=summer-30-2015" class="actionLinkLite">summer-30-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1300139222">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3720682403320153229">By the time I got to the end, I wanted to throw this book across the room, but by then I was exhausted. The book was too heavy to lift and heave properly, so I slapped the paperback covers with as much derision as I could manage.<br /><br />This is the longest book I’ve ever read. It’s the world’s 17th longest novel. Longer than <em>Infinite Jest</em>. Longer than <em>War and Peace</em>.<br /><br />You’d think they’d give me some sort of prize for reading all that. But what do I get instead? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[I get THAT ending? Some review</span></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3720682403320153229">By the time I got to the end, I wanted to throw this book across the room, but by then I was exhausted. The book was too heavy to lift and heave properly, so I slapped the paperback covers with as much derision as I could manage.<br /><br />This is the longest book I’ve ever read. It’s the world’s 17th longest novel. Longer than <em>Infinite Jest</em>. Longer than <em>War and Peace</em>.<br /><br />You’d think they’d give me some sort of prize for reading all that. But what do I get instead? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[I get THAT ending? Some reviewers congratulate Vikram Seth for not indulging the romantic notions of readers who want a happy ending for his two star-crossed lovers. That elevates <em>A Suitable Boy</em> above tawdry romance novels. The thing is, if I read a whole book only to have the heroine choose the easy, boring choice, <em>that is not a story</em>. That is just someone doing the obvious, pedestrian things we go through every day. I stuck with this story for 1500 pages because I wanted to see how the girl would end up with the perfect but tragically unsuitable boy. And she didn’t! I am so annoyed and heartbroken. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I was all set to give this book four stars. The boring parts—hundreds of pages of boring parts—would be forgiven because the good parts were so good. Ugh. But then I began turning those last pages with a sick, disgusted, wretched feeling. That cost the book two more stars. Now that I’m finished I have to keep telling myself it’s not real. It’s only a story. So then I should probably add a star back on because if it made me feel that emotional about it, that is effective. On some level. Not the best level, but I guess you can’t have everything.<br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3720682403320153229">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_164159050">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164159050" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5338330-shriya" class="left imgcol" title="Shriya"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1428331301p2/5338330.jpg" alt="Shriya" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/164159050?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 20, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5338330-shriya" class="user" title="Shriya">Shriya</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/10469712-a-suitable-boy" title="Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5338330-shriya?shelf=favourites" class="actionLinkLite">favourites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5338330-shriya?shelf=tome-travelling" class="actionLinkLite">tome-travelling</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5338330-shriya?shelf=books-i-own" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer164159050">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12871640656054890750"><strong> <em> A fact</em> </strong>: I never ever understood how postpartum depression works or why women suffer from it. <br /><br /><strong> <em> Yet another fact:</em> </strong> Having finished <em> A Suitable Boy</em> arouses similar feelings in a reader as postpartum depression in a new Mum. <br /><br /><em> Why? </em><br /><br />Well, by the you finish reading one of the longest English novels ever written and the longest English Novel written by an Indian and that Indian is Vikram Seth, you're kind of used to the story, the characters, the way their life goes on. So, when you turn the last pa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12871640656054890750"><strong> <em> A fact</em> </strong>: I never ever understood how postpartum depression works or why women suffer from it. <br /><br /><strong> <em> Yet another fact:</em> </strong> Having finished <em> A Suitable Boy</em> arouses similar feelings in a reader as postpartum depression in a new Mum. <br /><br /><em> Why? </em><br /><br />Well, by the you finish reading one of the longest English novels ever written and the longest English Novel written by an Indian and that Indian is Vikram Seth, you're kind of used to the story, the characters, the way their life goes on. So, when you turn the last page of something that has sprained your wrists for days, you certainly feel the sense of accomplishment which matches in effort if not in pain, to delivering a baby but at the same time you're depressed you'd NEVER be able to read this book again for the first time, that its time with you in that unique one to one bond, though cherished, will never be intimate in the same sense as before.<br /><br />Having expressed my feelings, thus, I will now proceed to review one of my favourite author's biggest masterpiece.<br /><br /><em> <strong> To all those who wonder and have asked me,</strong> "Is there a dull moment or dry spells in the book? </em>: NO! Not one! Not half a page and no, my blind love for Vikram Seth doesn't make me say so. In fact, as I said weeks ago about <a title="The Color Purple by Alice Walker" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11486.The_Color_Purple">The Color Purple</a>, it is as complete in every sense as a book could be. <br /><br />I love how Vikram Seth seems to have a laugh at everyone including himself. I love how his mother's life was the theme for this story. And I love how if you're remotely interested in anything in the world, be in Schubert or Classical Indian Music, Post Independence History or Indian Politics, Religion or Riots, English Lietrature or poems by Urdu/Arabic/Persian poets like Mast, Daagh, Minai or Rumi, you will not fail to love this book! <br /><br />Vikram Seth's characters are a class apart, supremely hilarious even in the gravest of situations, laughably filmy and over dramatic and yet as close to being real as characters could be. They don't claim to be perfect, they all have flaws, you will probably be angry at one or more of them during the course of the novel but you will not fail to love them despite all their faults!<br /><br /><em>Should you read it?</em><br /><br /> Certainly! I don't see why being daunted by the length of the novel, you should miss on something so exquisitely well written as this book. <br /><br /><em> Will you regret spending a thousand bucks/ a couple of pounds/ a few dollars? </em><br /><br /> Not at all if you claim to love literature for it is the finest piece of contemporary literature there is!<br /><br /><em> Any tip for how to go about it? </em><br /><br />1.If you're Indian, try and think of Bollywood film stars for every character. That makes the book even more fun and more lucid than it already is but that's entirely optional! <br /><br />2. Have someone else read it with you, a friend or someone from your book club. You need to keep discussing it and gushing about it with someone. It's like <em> Harry Potter</em> that way!<br /><br />More than just a good read! Rather, a BRILLIANT read and already my novel of the year! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12871640656054890750">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_101538881">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101538881" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2190636-joselito-honestly-and-brilliantly" class="left imgcol" title="Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1349701607p2/2190636.jpg" alt="Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/101538881?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 06, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2190636-joselito-honestly-and-brilliantly" class="user" title="Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly">Joselito Honestly and Brilliantly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer101538881">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10108693211019673014">This is like a buffet of Indian food. Everything seems to be here, in this monster of a book, all 1349 pages and 3 kilos of it: law, politics, business, history, tradition, superstitions, deities, romance, suspense, tragedy, humor, festivals, marriages, infidelities, friendship, betrayal, family, deaths, births, suicide,court trials, land reform, poetry, the Chatterji's couplets, amusing characters, etc. Even my mother is here (I mean, a character who, in some ways, resembles my mother). There's</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10108693211019673014">This is like a buffet of Indian food. Everything seems to be here, in this monster of a book, all 1349 pages and 3 kilos of it: law, politics, business, history, tradition, superstitions, deities, romance, suspense, tragedy, humor, festivals, marriages, infidelities, friendship, betrayal, family, deaths, births, suicide,court trials, land reform, poetry, the Chatterji's couplets, amusing characters, etc. Even my mother is here (I mean, a character who, in some ways, resembles my mother). There's something in it for everybody and this comprehensiveness makes it difficult for anyone not to like--or at least not to like something in--this book. Personally, I think the best here would be a tie between the love stories and Vikram Seth's wicked, humorous turn of phrase and the witty conversations between his characters which made me smile so many times.<br /><br />Even the heftiness of this book did not escape the author's humor. A character here, Amit, is also an author. In a scene somewhere near the end of the book Amit is entertaining some questions from a group of academicians after a poetry reading he held. One asks him about the novel he is writing which is rumoured to be more than a thousand page long already--<br /><br />"'Why, then, is it rumoured that your forthcoming novel--to be set, I understand, in Bengal--is to be so long? More than a thousand pages!' she exclaimed reproachfully, as if he were personally responsible for the nervous exhaustion of some future dissertationist.<br /><br />"'Oh, I don't know how it grew to be so long,' said Amit. 'I'm very undisciplined. But I too hate long books: the better, the worse. If they're bad, they merely make me pant with the effort of holding them up for a few minutes. But if they're good, I turn into a social moron for days, refusing to go out of my room, scowling and growling at interruptions, ignoring weddings and funerals, and making enemies out of friends. I still bear the scars of 'Middlemarch.'<br /><br />"'How about Proust?' asked a distracted-looking lady, who had begun knitting the moment the poems stopped.<br /><br />"Amit was surprised that anyone read Proust in Brahmpur. He had begun to feel rather happy, as if he had breathed in too much oxygen.<br /><br />"'I'm sure I'd love Proust,' he replied, 'if my mind was more like the Sundarbans: meandering, all-absorptive, endlessly, er, sub-reticulated. But as it is, Proust makes me weep, weep, weep with boredom. Weep', he added, He paused and sighed. "Weep, weep, weep,' he continued emphatically. 'I weep when I read Proust, and I read very little of him.'<br /><br />"There was a shocked silence: why should anyone feel so strongly about anything? It was broken by Professor Mishra.<br /><br />"'Needless to say, many of the most lasting monuments of literature are rather, well, bulky.' He smiled at Amit. 'Shakespeare is not merely great but grand, as it were.'<br /><br />"'But only as it were,' said Amit. 'He only looks big in bulk. And I have my own way of reducing that bulk,' he confided. 'You may have noticed that in a typical 'Collected Shakespeare' all the plays start on the right-hand side. Sometimes, the editors bung a picture in on the left to force them to do so. Well, what I do is to take my pen-knife and slit the whole book up into forty or so fascicles. That way I can roll up 'Hamlet' or 'Timon'--and slip them into my pocket. And when I'm wandering around--in a cemetery, say--I can take them out and read them. It's easy on the mind and on the wrists. I recommend it to everyone. I read 'Cymbeline' in just that way on the train here; and I never would have otherwise.'"<br /><br />Vikram Seth may not be aversed to the idea of his book being torn up for easy reading like what his character Amit did to his 'Shakespeares'. But whether you do that or not, you will not weep, weep, weep while reading 'A Suitable Boy.' This is a delightful work of art.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10108693211019673014">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_725667950">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/725667950" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3131238-judy" class="left imgcol" title="Judy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1358272075p2/3131238.jpg" alt="Judy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/725667950?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 06, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3131238-judy" class="user" title="Judy">Judy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">around the world readers</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3131238-judy?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3131238-judy?shelf=chunksters" class="actionLinkLite">chunksters</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3131238-judy?shelf=india" class="actionLinkLite">india</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3131238-judy?shelf=2013-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2013-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer725667950">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17692658373896985522">I'm feeling this great sense of accomplishment right now after finishing this gargantuan book this morning. The crazy thing is that I almost wish it wasn't done. I want to know so many things about the characters - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ did Varun get it together now that he finally made it through his civil service exams, did anything come of him and Kalpana? Is Malati wedging in between that relationship? So many unanswered questions! (sigh) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> However, I thoroughly enjoyed this book, co</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17692658373896985522">I'm feeling this great sense of accomplishment right now after finishing this gargantuan book this morning. The crazy thing is that I almost wish it wasn't done. I want to know so many things about the characters - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ did Varun get it together now that he finally made it through his civil service exams, did anything come of him and Kalpana? Is Malati wedging in between that relationship? So many unanswered questions! (sigh) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> However, I thoroughly enjoyed this book, cover-to-cover and would love to see a sequel, A Suitable Girl, all about Varun and his quest for love!<br /><br />This book is an excellent companion to the other wonderful (chunkster-size)India-reading that I have done the last couple of years: <a title="A Fine Balance by Rohinton Mistry" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5211.A_Fine_Balance">A Fine Balance</a> and <a title="The Toss of a Lemon by Padma Viswanathan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2694064.The_Toss_of_a_Lemon">The Toss of a Lemon</a>. While <a title="A Suitable Boy (A Suitable Boy, #1) by Vikram Seth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy__A_Suitable_Boy___1_">A Suitable Boy</a> offers an excellent look at post-partition India, it also touched on the touchiness of what was suppose to be a caste-free India. There is clearly progress made in that direction particularly with the younger people and the more educated adults, most of the hold-outs are older people such as Mrs. Tandor, it is evident that it will be a problem a long time to come since Indian society is built on this ugly system. <br /><br />Seth does a wonderful job with his characters - the manipulative, but loveable Mrs. Mehra to the liberated Malati to the arrogant, insecure Arun to the lovely Lata to the ambitious Haresh.<br /><br />Speaking of the search for the "Suitable Boy", the chase was a fun one. Although originally I told myself I would be disappointed if Lata picked anyone other than <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ her true love, Kabir, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I could not fault her final choice or her reasons for picking him. I was surprised with how much I concurred and didn't feel the sense of disappointment expected. So, all-in-all - good book, I recommend without hesitation, especially to around-the-world readers. Don't let the size of this book intimidate you into picking it up, just think of it as a trilogy that you will be reading all at once!<br /><br />4.5 stars<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17692658373896985522">...more</a>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/2074287-prashant-r" class="left imgcol" title="Prashant R"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Prashant R" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/47574103?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 26, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2074287-prashant-r" class="user" title="Prashant R">Prashant R</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer47574103">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer322737737184239062">I read this book, almost two decades ago, when it first released in 1991. I had just appeared for my 12th grade exams and was hungrily soaking up books, through my vacations. I borrowed it from my neighborhood "circulating" library in Bombay, for a princely sum of Rs 50/- (a single US $). This was also the first book by an Indian author i had read.The scope, the breadth and the range of characters, in this book, are breathtaking. I could associate with some of the characters and certainly the mi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText322737737184239062">I read this book, almost two decades ago, when it first released in 1991. I had just appeared for my 12th grade exams and was hungrily soaking up books, through my vacations. I borrowed it from my neighborhood "circulating" library in Bombay, for a princely sum of Rs 50/- (a single US $). This was also the first book by an Indian author i had read.The scope, the breadth and the range of characters, in this book, are breathtaking. I could associate with some of the characters and certainly the milieu. I took me,two weeks to devour this book. And i loved the book.<br /><br />This book holds special memories for me This is the first book, i have bought from my first salary, in 1996. I also met Vikram Seth when he was at a promotional event for his book "Two Lives" in Chicago, in 2007. He autographed my copy of "Two Lives" and he also signed for my copy of "The Suitable Boy", when i told him about how special his book was for me.<br /><br />I realize, that this is more a general "Suitable Boy" ramble, then a review. But really how many such books exist, which weave themselves irrevocably into your lives. I want to re-read this sometime. Waiting for a sabbatical or my retirement.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="322737737184239062">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8068346656184740517">A Suitable boy is a very sutiable book for both boys &amp; girls.. <br /><br />When I borrowed this book from the library I found it surprisingly huge and scary, everyone who saw me carrying it was equally astounded. I started having my doubts that what if the book becomes a lousy read and I end up wasting my time or leave it half read.. but the book from Page 1 had a smooth pace &amp; never for once lost my interest. SO when Vikram Seth says in his opening lines.. <br /><br />'Buy me before good sense insists,<br />You’ll s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8068346656184740517">A Suitable boy is a very sutiable book for both boys &amp; girls.. <br /><br />When I borrowed this book from the library I found it surprisingly huge and scary, everyone who saw me carrying it was equally astounded. I started having my doubts that what if the book becomes a lousy read and I end up wasting my time or leave it half read.. but the book from Page 1 had a smooth pace &amp; never for once lost my interest. SO when Vikram Seth says in his opening lines.. <br /><br />'Buy me before good sense insists,<br />You’ll strain your purse and sprain your wrists.'<br /><br />he is not right but not also wrong.. though I didn spend money on it and though heavy &amp; huge - I could manage without straining my wrists.. But you know what - this book is collecter's item so buy it and save it.. sutiable for your library.<br /><br />To read more:<br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://storywala.blogspot.in/2011/12/suitable-book.html" target="_blank">http://storywala.blogspot.in/2011/12/...</a><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer373675792">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6245429238265934351">How do I review this book? It is long...1,350 pages long...which for this book is TOO long.<br />It is heavy...as in 4 1/2 pounds heavy...and not available in an e-book version. <br />I built up my forearm muscles and strained my wrists reading all 1,350 pages of this 4 1/2 pound monstrosity.<br /><br />As to the contents of the book...did I mention it is TOO long. It was interesting, yes, but too detailed for its own good. The novel covers a year in the life of four familes in India in the 1950's. The story of Lata an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6245429238265934351">How do I review this book? It is long...1,350 pages long...which for this book is TOO long.<br />It is heavy...as in 4 1/2 pounds heavy...and not available in an e-book version. <br />I built up my forearm muscles and strained my wrists reading all 1,350 pages of this 4 1/2 pound monstrosity.<br /><br />As to the contents of the book...did I mention it is TOO long. It was interesting, yes, but too detailed for its own good. The novel covers a year in the life of four familes in India in the 1950's. The story of Lata and her mother's search to find her a "suitable boy" to marry I enjoyed. The story of Mann and his adventures good and bad I enjoyed. The long, detailed dissertations of the political culture of a newly independent India I could have used a bit less detail on.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6245429238265934351">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_933080895">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/933080895" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10712882-joy-stephenson" class="left imgcol" title="Joy Stephenson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1376040776p2/10712882.jpg" alt="Joy Stephenson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/933080895?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 10, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10712882-joy-stephenson" class="user" title="Joy Stephenson">Joy Stephenson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer933080895">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer298718731112638489">This is a story about relationships – romantic, among families, between friends, in political groups, between religious faiths and sectors of society (including castes). It deals with the conflict between personal freedom / self-fulfilment and duty / responsibility towards others. It is a long and complex novel, in which the stories of the different groups of characters are skilfully plaited together to make a multi-faceted tale. One of the strengths of the book is that each time we return to a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText298718731112638489">This is a story about relationships – romantic, among families, between friends, in political groups, between religious faiths and sectors of society (including castes). It deals with the conflict between personal freedom / self-fulfilment and duty / responsibility towards others. It is a long and complex novel, in which the stories of the different groups of characters are skilfully plaited together to make a multi-faceted tale. One of the strengths of the book is that each time we return to a character, while he or she may have changed or developed as a person, they behave – not as we would expect exactly, because that would make it boring – but consistent with their nature and experience. No character is wholly good or bad; they are real people. The story doesn't offer any easy answers; decisions made on both the personal and political level have repercussions and sometimes all a character can do is act in a way to cause the least harm. Although this is a very long novel, the pace is excellent with high drama balanced by humour, poignant sadness with joy. This is the second time I have read this book and if anything I enjoyed it even more this time, some 15 years later.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="298718731112638489">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_79570737">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79570737" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1521829-chris" class="left imgcol" title="Chris"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1432561615p2/1521829.jpg" alt="Chris" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/79570737?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 13, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1521829-chris" class="user" title="Chris">Chris</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1521829-chris?shelf=2010-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2010-reads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1521829-chris?shelf=best-of-2010" class="actionLinkLite">best-of-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer79570737'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer79570737">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1454482747590481674">ATTENTION: SMALL SPOILERS AT THE END!<br /><br />This book literally had it all: love, intrigue, death, birth, lust, suspense, comedy, sibling rivalry, politics, religion, history, all with an overly dramatic mom. While I didn't give this five stars because I loved the book, I gave it five stars because of its complexity. This wasn't just a story, I was transferred to India circa 1951. It totally envelopes you in the story. While the backbone is Lata's quest for "a suitable boy" you become a member of the f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1454482747590481674">ATTENTION: SMALL SPOILERS AT THE END!<br /><br />This book literally had it all: love, intrigue, death, birth, lust, suspense, comedy, sibling rivalry, politics, religion, history, all with an overly dramatic mom. While I didn't give this five stars because I loved the book, I gave it five stars because of its complexity. This wasn't just a story, I was transferred to India circa 1951. It totally envelopes you in the story. While the backbone is Lata's quest for "a suitable boy" you become a member of the four families. It took me quite some time to finally get the families' names straight, who was with which family and married to whom, as there were some marriages that crossed between them. Even on the morning I finished this, I still paged back to the family trees. <br /><br />There were so many different stories going on at the same time, but Seth smartly sprinkled them throughout the book. If you get bored, have no fear, you'll move on to something else soon enough. Each "chapter" or couplet as he had, usually had two stories that he seamlessly wove together, so much so it was a few pages in before I realized we had moved on to another part of the story. <br /><br />His writing? Eh, was a bit disappointed. I adored "An Equal Music," and part of that was his lyrical writing. Heck, I even picked up the violin for about a year because I was so intrigued about the music quartet! This almost felt like it was translated to me, although I know it wasn't. Was stilted in parts, and not one of a finessed writer, although this may have been one of his first books. <br /><br />The problem of having a book this long is it's like time, you start to forget what happened in the beginning. I felt that way halfway through, I had to keep reminding myself of certain things that happened to some of the characters. <br /><br />To end, I'll put in two small spoilers. I was SO disappointed with the boy Lata marries. How I wanted her to end up with Kabir. Ah, unrequited love, and I'm always looking for that happy ending. Also, I felt that Vikram Seth was the poet, Amit=. There were a couple of things that lead me to think that. <br /><br />A couple of friends asked me the other day should they read it. I wouldn't recommend a 1,000-plus page book, as something this long is truly an investment, even for someone who reads a lot. Do I think it was worth it? Whenever I am involved in a book, I always wonder what is happening with the characters when I close the cover, and I know I will wonder about these four families. Is Lata happy in her marriage? How is Maan doing? Is Parvati's baby born? I spent the past two months with these people, and for the most part, I liked them all. I'm not jumping up and down for joy (well, maybe because I can read something else!) that this book was so incredible, it was too complex and detailed for me to do that. But yes, it was worth it. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1454482747590481674">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/538557289?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 18, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10051121-sadaf" class="user" title="Sadaf">Sadaf</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer538557289">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17429879495856903799">I love this book. If I had to choose my favourite book of all times, perhaps this one would win it. <br />I don't know what exactly is the reason for loving it so. Maybe its because my life situations are similar to the protagonist Lata in the book. Or because of the tender yet moving way in which the book is written. Or the proper timing of humour in the book, or the interesting plot. Maybe its all of that together. <br />The book begins with Lata at her sister Savita's wedding, where we come to know of La</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17429879495856903799">I love this book. If I had to choose my favourite book of all times, perhaps this one would win it. <br />I don't know what exactly is the reason for loving it so. Maybe its because my life situations are similar to the protagonist Lata in the book. Or because of the tender yet moving way in which the book is written. Or the proper timing of humour in the book, or the interesting plot. Maybe its all of that together. <br />The book begins with Lata at her sister Savita's wedding, where we come to know of Lata's exact situation, her times, her family. As the story goes further, we meet Kabir, a handsome young boy from Lata's college, with whom she soon falls in love. <br />Set in Calcutta, Delhi, Brahmpur and Salimpur, the book is not only about Lata, but many people around her, and about many things, from love to politics to family and religion. <br />Later in the book Lata meets Amit, a writer, and Haresh, a hard-working young fellow in a prestigious Shoe manufacturing company. <br />By the end of the book, as each of the issues get sorted, only one question remains, whom will Lata marry? Kabir, Amit or Haresh? <br />The book ends perfectly, and every reader is bound to love as well as be puzzled by her decision. <br />The book takes one back to simpler times. The sequel to it, A Suitable Girl, or An Unsuitable Boy, will come out this year, and I eagerly await it.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1475989566">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1475989566" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/47239298-faroukh-naseem" class="left imgcol" title="Faroukh Naseem"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452493429p2/47239298.jpg" alt="Faroukh Naseem" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1475989566?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/47239298-faroukh-naseem" class="user" title="Faroukh Naseem">Faroukh Naseem</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1475989566">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13594032497400483729">I have always been impressed and awed by writers mainly because of the research and effort they put in to write the perfect tale and their imagination in bringing together characters and the details that govern each characters features...<br /><br />Vikram Seth has to be applauded for his effort (which seems to be such a petty word) when we talk about this Herculean book!<br /><br />**Extremely Mild Spoilers**<br /><br />The Basic plot is about Mrs. Rupa Mehra wanting to find a Suitable Boy for her youngest daughter, Lata but the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13594032497400483729">I have always been impressed and awed by writers mainly because of the research and effort they put in to write the perfect tale and their imagination in bringing together characters and the details that govern each characters features...<br /><br />Vikram Seth has to be applauded for his effort (which seems to be such a petty word) when we talk about this Herculean book!<br /><br />**Extremely Mild Spoilers**<br /><br />The Basic plot is about Mrs. Rupa Mehra wanting to find a Suitable Boy for her youngest daughter, Lata but the story dwells into a lot lot more...Politics, Religion, intolerance, Shoe Making, Farming, Teaching...its like he has described what India literally would have felt like through the eyes of Mothers, daughters, ministers, Royals (Nawabs), Religious people, Actors, Musicians...You name it and VS has given you at least a hint on their insights to India.<br /><br />At its heart it really is about India, and how India deals with suddenly having to take care of itself instead of being told how to 'take care' of itself by the British....<br /><br />The way minute details are dealt with is exemplary and the vocabulary used is very easy to comprehend although some words were totally new to me.<br /><br />The way he understood Islamic laws for example prove the detailed manner in which he must have spoken to religious scholars. And how he describes the shoe making process starting from the sacrifice of the animal...to the finished product...<br /><br />The chapters are long (80 pages approx) and they swing between Brahmpur/Calcutta/Delhi/Kanpur.<br /><br />The court scenes really bored me and more so because i reached the first one on a weekend where i excitedly woke up at 6 to read.<br /><br />I've never really appreciated poetry because of the cheesiness but i loved some of the poetry included in the book (and VS being a poet couldn't refrain from including dozens) , And i was glad!<br /><br />Some of the characters you long for while reading and VS made sure you cant get enough of so many of them.<br /><br />One Character i was so excited about was Zainab but she doesn't really show up later in the book.<br /><br />My favorites were and you will know why when you read the book - Maan, Zainab's Cameo, Dipankar, Saeeda Begum, Dr. Durrani, Rasheed.<br /><br />But my absolute favorite hands down was Mrs Rupa Mehra. I have used so many tags to mark pages of hers...! The way i could picture so many of my aunts acting like Rupa Mehra was hilarious....!<br /><br />That is one fictional Character i could literally relate someone to :) <br /><br />I don't want to get into too much details and spoil a mammoth book for anyone of you who might be interested in giving away at least a month of your reading time...But i really wish people would read such books to give them not just a great reading experience but a lifetime experience about how life has always been complicated, not just for us but our parents and theirs...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13594032497400483729">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_671180982">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/671180982" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2006699-tariq-mahmood" class="left imgcol" title="Tariq Mahmood"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1316115355p2/2006699.jpg" alt="Tariq Mahmood" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/671180982?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 06, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2006699-tariq-mahmood" class="user" title="Tariq Mahmood">Tariq Mahmood</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/789684.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9781857990881" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2006699-tariq-mahmood?shelf=india" class="actionLinkLite">india</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer671180982">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17195712789402396764">Some are born mad, some achieve madness, and others have madness thrust upon them.<br />The book is set in the days just after partition, based on families going through birth pangs after the Partition of India into India and Pakistan. The Partition and subsequent religious riots in India have made a pretty significant affect on the psych of India which is of a much more lasting nature than Pakistan who can only look back or read about Partition on their end. Indians on the other hand live in constant</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17195712789402396764">Some are born mad, some achieve madness, and others have madness thrust upon them.<br />The book is set in the days just after partition, based on families going through birth pangs after the Partition of India into India and Pakistan. The Partition and subsequent religious riots in India have made a pretty significant affect on the psych of India which is of a much more lasting nature than Pakistan who can only look back or read about Partition on their end. Indians on the other hand live in constant fear of inciting yet another religious riot in their cities while Pakistanis can move on after burying the riots behind them. Religious riots are far more dangerous than racial riots.<br /><br />It struck me almost halfway through the novel, the irony of the much lauded Zamindari bill which Seth has so vividly portrayed in this classic novel. What is the difference between the East India Company and the Indian Nationalists if the All India Congress party? The Zamindari bill was same policy polished and re-badged all over again. How can we have the audacity to accuse the British of exploiting India when Indians seem to have done exactly the same when their turn was up?<br /><br />As I read more and more of this wondrously engaging story, I could relate to straight parables to the Partition drama, there is a crime of drunken passion purported by one good friend, which for me resembled the senseless riots after the Partition. There are other examples which are steeped in Partition which for me makes the story very relevant for a proper depiction of that era. <br /><br /><br />All in all the book was a very engaging read. The only drawback was the size of the paperback which makes it a very difficult job to lunge around, but I am not taking any stars from because of it....</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17195712789402396764">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_11860501">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11860501" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/607125-lulu" class="left imgcol" title="Lulu"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1195087002p2/607125.jpg" alt="Lulu" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/11860501?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 11, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/607125-lulu" class="user" title="Lulu">Lulu</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/50365.A_Suitable_Boy" title="Paperback 9780060786526" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer11860501'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer11860501">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10254291903693922068">I finally finished it. Overall, it was a good read but I can't say that it was one of my favorites.<br /><br />1. It was too long. The stories could have been told in a more succinct way. This includes the politics. I found myself constantly re-reading those sections.<br />2. The author should have included a glossary to define some of the terms he used or used the words in a way that I could figure out what he was talking about. In some places he did this but not nearly enough and so I found myself trying to fig</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10254291903693922068">I finally finished it. Overall, it was a good read but I can't say that it was one of my favorites.<br /><br />1. It was too long. The stories could have been told in a more succinct way. This includes the politics. I found myself constantly re-reading those sections.<br />2. The author should have included a glossary to define some of the terms he used or used the words in a way that I could figure out what he was talking about. In some places he did this but not nearly enough and so I found myself trying to figure it out and eventually, specially in the final 300 pages so moving on, only to realize that it was not necessary to know what he was talking about.<br />3. There was a lot of information about politics, religion, cultural norms as they relate to a class but I don't feel that I understand it better now as a result. There is a lot of information in my head but I can't make sense of it.<br />4. I felt that some of the characters were intentionally, by the author, portrayed in a certain light and all with the goal of leading Lata, the main character to her choice in the end. I noticed this from the beginning when Lata had a conversation with Malati about her future choice. At that point, I knew what her choice would be but continued reading the remaining 1400 pages anyway. Savita was there as the light to lead Lata in case she got "lost". Arun was portrayed as the fool of the family. Really clueless of himself being a pawn at his employer and self-absorbed in the status it represented. This I believe was the nail on the coffin for Lata's decision.<br />5. There were characters that were very interesting but the author ran out of time to finish their stories. I cared more about them and in the end was disappointed that I will never know what became of them. I can insinuate about Maan, Malati and Firoz (among others) but then it would be my story and not the authors.<br /><br />Maybe one day I will read it again and perhaps spend more time on the politics and less on the characters. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10254291903693922068">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//&lt;![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('js8qkxv/STojx9E+9/QmgQRf9ASCiMlhkSdut+LOGOHrGxVA6S1dwK8fpYWJlcAzTag3HctVjsv7LmslLlvupA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8CieeMgiu0zA3TJqqEJ6kR4o1YqoLcStJuDQ292p49yV/KGrOvCvtkwFRtHWI5wjV98Wk+HwgwdM6dVJETwVmQ==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

But in this city redolent of timeworn customs, where pilgrims bathe in the sacred Ganges and breathe in smoke from burning ghats along the shore, Samar is offered entirely different perspectives on his country. Miss West and her circle, indifferent to the reality around them, represent those drawn to India as a respite from the material world. And Rajesh, a sometimes violent, sometimes mystical leader of student malcontents, presents a more jaundiced view. Young Lenny Sethi is kept out of school because she suffers from polio. She spends her days with Ayah, her beautiful nanny, visiting with the large group of admirers that Ayah draws. It is in the company of these working class characters that Lenny learns about religious differences, religious intolerance, and the blossoming genocidal strife on the eve of Partition. As she matures, Lenny begins to identify the differences between the Hindus, Moslems, and Sikhs engaging in political arguments all around her. Lenny enjoys a happy, privileged life in Lahore, but the kidnapping of her beloved Ayah signals a dramatic change. Soon Lenny’s world erupts in religious, ethnic, and racial violence. At the center of the narrative is the character of Vishnu, an aging alcoholic houseboy on the precipice of death, who lies, penniless, on the bottom step of a middle-class Bombay apartment house. While Vishnu appears to face his impending death placidly and philosophically, a maelstrom swirls around him. The residents of the building include a reclusive widower mourning the untimely death of his young wife, a Moslem family coping with the daily prejudices of their Hindu neighbors, and two families who unhappily share a kitchen. Worlds collide when the Moslem family\'s son elopes with the Hindu family\'s daughter, and Mr. Jalal, the Moslem family patriarch, apparently flips his wig, recognizing Vishnu not as their dying houseboy but as the deity whose name he bears, with the power to save. And when Mr. Jalal is found sleeping on the stairs beside Vishnu, he becomes the scapegoat for the building\'s many ills. In its frenetic and hilarious conclusion, The Death of Vishnu trumpets the arrival of an extremely gifted Indian writer, bringing to spectacular life the tempestuous chaos that is life in India today. Kirkpatrick had gone out to India as an ambitious soldier in the army of the East India Company, eager to make his name in the conquest and subjection of the subcontinent. Instead, he fell in love with Khair and overcame many obstacles to marry her—not least of which was the fact that she was locked away in purdah and engaged to a local nobleman. Eventually, while remaining Resident, Kirkpatrick converted to Islam, and according to Indian sources even became a double-agent working for the Hyderabadis against the East India Company.\n\nIt is a remarkable story, involving secret assignations, court intrigue, harem politics, religious and family disputes. But such things were not unknown; from the early sixteenth century, when the Inquisition banned the Portuguese in Goa from wearing the dhoti, to the eve of the Indian mutiny, the \'white Mughals\' who wore local dress and adopted Indian ways were a source of embarrassments to successive colonial administrations. William Dalrymple unearths such colourful figures as \'Hindoo Stuart\', who travelled with his own team of Brahmins to maintain his temple of idols, and who spent many years trying to persuade the memsahibs of Calcutta to adopt the sari; and Sir David Ochterlony, Kirkpatrick\'s counterpart in Delhi, who took all thirteen of his wives out for evening promenades, each on the back of their own elephant.\n\nIn White Mughals, William Dalrymple discovers a world almost entirely unexplored by history, and places at its centre a compelling tale of love, seduction and betrayal. It possesses all the sweep and resonance of a great nineteenth-century novel, set against a background of shifting alliances and the manoeuvring of the great powers, the mercantile ambitions of the British and the imperial dreams of Napoleon. White Mughals, the product of five years\' writing and research, triumphantly confirms Dalrymple\'s reputation as one of the finest writers at work today.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/28345.Vikram_Seth">About Vikram Seth</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/28345.Vikram_Seth"><img alt="28345" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1293504690p2/28345.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer5103161893593376777">Vikram Seth is an Indian poet, novelist, travel writer, librettist, children's writer, biographer and memoirist. <br /><br />During the course of his doctorate studies at Stanford, he did his field work in China and translated Hindi and Chinese poetry into English. He returned to Delhi via Xinjiang and Tibet which led to a travel narrative <em>From Heaven Lake: Travels Through Sinkiang and Tibet</em> (1983) which won</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5103161893593376777">Vikram Seth is an Indian poet, novelist, travel writer, librettist, children's writer, biographer and memoirist. <br /><br />During the course of his doctorate studies at Stanford, he did his field work in China and translated Hindi and Chinese poetry into English. He returned to Delhi via Xinjiang and Tibet which led to a travel narrative <em>From Heaven Lake: Travels Through Sinkiang and Tibet</em> (1983) which won the Thomas Cook Travel Book Award.<br /><br /><em>The Golden Gate: A Novel in Verse</em> (1986) was his first novel describing the experiences of a group of friends who live in California. <em>A Suitable Boy</em> (1993), an epic of Indian life set in the 1950s, got him the WH Smith Literary Award and the Commonwealth Writers Prize. <br /><br />His poetry includes <em>The Humble Administrator's Garden</em> (1985) and <em>All You Who Sleep Tonight</em> (1990). His <em>Beastly Tales from Here and There</em> (1992) is children's book consisting of ten stories in verse about animals.<br /><br />In 2005, he published <em>Two Lives</em>, a family memoir written at the suggestion of his mother, which focuses on the lives of his great-uncle (Shanti Behari Seth) and German-Jewish great aunt (Henny Caro) who met in Berlin in the early 1930s while Shanti was a student there and with whom Seth stayed extensively on going to England at age 17 for school. As with <em>From Heaven Lake</em>, <em>Two Lives</em> contains much autobiography.<br /><br />An unusually forthcoming writer whose published material is replete with un- or thinly-disguised details as to the personal lives of himself and his intimates related in a highly engaging narrative voice, Seth has said that he is somewhat perplexed that his readers often in consequence presume to an unwelcome degree of personal familiarity with him.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5103161893593376777">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/28345.Vikram_Seth" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Vikram Seth...</a>

Set in the early 1950s in an India newly independ&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText4111911372959652604\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;Vikram Seth\'s novel is, at its core, a love story: the tale of Lata\'s--and her mother, Mrs. Rupa Mehra\'s--attempts to find a suitable boy for Lata, through love or through exacting maternal appraisal. Set in the early 1950s in an India newly independent and struggling through a time of crisis, A Suitable Boy takes us into the richly imagined world of four large extended families and spins a compulsively readable tale of their lives and loves. A sweeping panoramic portrait of a complex, multiethnic society in flux, A Suitable Boy remains the story of ordinary people caught up in a web of love and ambition, humor and sadness, prejudice and       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1651078-a-suitable-boy">Quotes from A Suitable Boy</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“God save us from people who mean well.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/150628-god-save-us-from-people-who-mean-well" class="actionLinkLite">1642 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“But I too hate long books: the better, the worse. If they're bad they merely make me pant with the effort of holding them up for a few minutes. But if they're good, I turn into a social moron for days, refusing to go out of my room, scowling and growling at interruptions, ignoring weddings and funerals, and making enemies out of friends. I still bear the scars of Middlemarch.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/110695-but-i-too-hate-long-books-the-better-the-worse" class="actionLinkLite">167 likes</a>
